\t}\n618: \n619: \t// Refresh!\n620: \tpriorVal := state.Value\n621: \n622: \t// Unmarked before sending to provider\n623: \tvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\n624: \tif priorVal.ContainsMarked() set for this resource, we don't want to talk\n631: \t\t// to the provider so we'll just return whatever was in state.\n632: \t\tresp = providers.ReadResourceResponse{\n633: \t\t\tNewState: priorVal,\n634: \t\t}\n635: \t} else {\n636: \t\tresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n637: \t\t\tTypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n638: \t\t\tPriorState:   priorVal,\n639: \t\t\tPrivate:      state.Private,\n640: \t\t\tProviderMeta: metaConfigVal,\n641: \t\t})\n642: \t}\n643: \tif n.Config != nil {\n644: \t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(n.Config.Config, n.Addr.String())\n645: \t}\n646: \n647: \tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics)\n648: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n649: \t\treturn state, diags\n650: \t}\n651: \n652: \tif resp.NewState == cty.NilVal {\n653: \t\t// This ought not to happen in real cases since it's not possible to\n654: \t\t// send NilVal over the plugin RPC channel, but it can come up in\n655: \t\t// tests due to sloppy mocking.\n656: \t\tpanic(\"new state is cty.NilVal\")\n657: \t}\n658: \n659: \tif !resp.NewState.IsWhollyKnown() {\n660: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n661: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n662: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n663: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n664: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n665: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, \"The returned state contains unknown values\",\n666: \t\t\t),\n667: \t\t))\n668: \t}\n669: \n670: \tfor _, err := range resp.NewState.Type().TestConformance(schema.ImpliedType()) {\n671: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n672: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n673: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n674: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n675: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n676: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, tfdiags.FormatError(err),\n677: \t\t\t),\n678: \t\t))\n679: \t}\n680: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n681: \t\treturn state, diags\n682: \t}\n683: \n684: \tnewState := objchange.NormalizeObjectFromLegacySDK(resp.NewState, schema)\n685: \tif !newState.RawEquals(resp.NewState) {\n686: \t\t// We had to fix up this object in some way, and we still need to\n687: \t\t// accept any changes for compatibility, so all we can do is log a\n688: \t\t// warning about the change.\n689: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[WARN] Provider %q produced an invalid new value containing null blocks for %q during refresh\\n\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr)\n690: \t}\n691: \n692: \tret := state.DeepCopy()\n693: \tret.Value = newState\n694: \tret.Private = resp.Private\n695: \n696: \t// We have no way to exempt provider using the legacy SDK from this check,\n697: \t// so we can only log inconsistencies with the updated state values.\n698: \t// In most cases these are not errors anyway, and represent \"drift\" from\n699: \t// external changes which will be handled by the subsequent plan.\n700: \tif errs := objchange.AssertObjectCompatible(schema, priorVal, ret.Value); len(errs) > 0 {\n701: \t\tvar buf strings.Builder\n702: \t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"[WARN] Provider %q produced an unexpected new value for %s during refresh.\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider.String(), absAddr)\n703: \t\tfor _, err := range errs {\n704: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"\\n      - %s\", tfdiags.FormatError(err))\n705: \t\t}\n706: \t\tlog.Print(buf.String())\n707: \t}\n708: \n709: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n710: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n711: \t\treturn h.PostRefresh(absAddr, deposedKey, priorVal, ret.Value)\n712: \t}))\n713: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n714: \t\treturn ret, diags\n715: \t}\n716: \n717: \t// Mark the value if necessary\n718: \tif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n719: \t\tret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n720: \t}\n721: \n722: \treturn ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n732: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n733: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n734: \n735: \tresource := n.Addr.Resource.Resource\n736: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n737: \tif err != nil {\n738: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n739: \t}\n740: \n741: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(resource)\n742: \tif schema == nil {\n743: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n744: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", resource.Type))\n745: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n746: \t}\n747: \n748: \t// If we're importing and generating config, generate it now.\n749: \tif n.Config == nil {\n750: \t\t// This shouldn't happen. A node that isn't generating config should\n751: \t\t// have embedded config, and the rest of Terraform should enforce this.\n752: \t\t// If, however, we didn't do things correctly the next line will panic,\n753: \t\t// so let's not do that and return an error message with more context.\n754: \n755: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n756: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n757: \t\t\t\"Resource has no configuration\",\n758: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Terraform attempted to process a resource at %s that has no configuration. This is a bug in Terraform; please report it!\", n.Addr.String())))\n759: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n760: \t}\n761: \n762: \tconfig := *n.Config\n763: \n764: \tcheckRuleSeverity := tfdiags.Error\n765: \tif n.preDestroyRefresh {\n766: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity = tfdiags.Warning\n767: \t}\n768: \n769: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n770: \t\t// If we already planned the action, we stick to that plan\n771: \t\tcreateBeforeDestroy = plannedChange.Action == plans.CreateThenDelete\n772: \t}\n773: \n774: \t// Evaluate the configuration\n775: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(n.Config.ForEach, ctx)\n776: \n777: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n778: \n779: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n780: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n781: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n782: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n783: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n784: \t)\n785: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n786: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n787: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed preconditions prevent further evaluation\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \t// If we have a previous plan and the action was a noop, then the only\n791: \t// reason we're in this method was to evaluate the preconditions. There's\n792: \t// no need to re-plan this resource.\n793: \tif plannedChange != nil && plannedChange.Action == plans.NoOp {\n794: \t\treturn plannedChange, currentState.DeepCopy(), keyData, diags\n795: \t}\n796: \n797: \torigConfigVal, _, configDiags := ctx.EvaluateBlock(config.Config, schema, nil, keyData)\n798: \tdiags = diags.Append(configDiags)\n799: \tif configDiags.HasErrors() {\n800: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n801: \t}\n802: \n803: \tmetaConfigVal, metaDiags := n.providerMetas(ctx)\n804: \tdiags = diags.Append(metaDiags)\n805: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n806: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n807: \t}\n808: \n809: \tvar priorVal cty.Value\n810: \tvar priorValTainted cty.Value\n811: \tvar priorPrivate []byte\n812: \tif currentState != nil {\n813: \t\tif currentState.Status != states.ObjectTainted {\n814: \t\t\tpriorVal = currentState.Value\n815: \t\t\tpriorPrivate = currentState.Private\n816: \t\t} else {\n817: \t\t\t// If the prior state is tainted then we'll proceed below like\n818: \t\t\t// we're creating an entirely new object, but then turn it into\n819: \t\t\t// a synthetic \"Replace\" change at the end, creating the same\n820: \t\t\t// result as if the provider had marked at least one argument\n821: \t\t\t// change as \"requires replacement\".\n822: \t\t\tpriorValTainted = currentState.Value\n823: \t\t\tpriorVal = cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n824: \t\t}\n825: \t} else {\n826: \t\tpriorVal = cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n827: \t}\n828: \n829: \tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Re-validating config for %q\", n.Addr)\n830: \t// Allow the provider to validate the final set of values.  The config was\n831: \t// statically validated early on, but there may have been unknown values\n832: \t// which the provider could not validate at the time.\n833: \t//\n834: \t// TODO: It would be more correct to validate the config after\n835: \t// ignore_changes has been applied, but the current implementation cannot\n836: \t// exclude computed-only attributes when given the `all` option.\n837: \n838: \t// we must unmark and use the original config, since the ignore_changes\n839: \t// handling below needs access to the marks.\n840: \tunmarkedConfigVal, _ := origConfigVal.UnmarkDeep()\n841: \tvalidateResp := provider.ValidateResourceConfig(\n842: \t\tproviders.ValidateResourceConfigRequest{\n843: \t\t\tTypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n844: \t\t\tConfig:   unmarkedConfigVal,\n845: \t\t},\n846: \t)\n847: \tdiags = diags.Append(validateResp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(config.Config, n.Addr.String()))\n848: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n849: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n850: \t}\n851: \n852: \t// ignore_changes is meant to only apply to the configuration, so it must\n853: \t// be applied before we generate a plan. This ensures the config used for\n854: \t// the proposed value, the proposed value itself, and the config presented\n855: \t// to the provider in the PlanResourceChange request all agree on the\n856: \t// starting values.\n857: \t// Here we operate on the marked values, so as to revert any changes to the\n858: \t// marks as well as the value.\n859: \tconfigValIgnored, ignoreChangeDiags := n.processIgnoreChanges(priorVal, origConfigVal, schema)\n860: \tdiags = diags.Append(ignoreChangeDiags)\n861: \tif ignoreChangeDiags.HasErrors() {\n862: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n863: \t}\n864: \n865: \t// Create an unmarked version of our config val and our prior val.\n866: \t// Store the paths for the config val to re-mark after we've sent things\n867: \t// over the wire.\n868: \tunmarkedConfigVal, unmarkedPaths := configValIgnored.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n869: \tunmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n870: \n871: \tproposedNewVal := objchange.ProposedNew(schema, unmarkedPriorVal, unmarkedConfigVal)\n872: \n873: \t// Call pre-diff hook\n874: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n875: \t\treturn h.PreDiff(n.Addr, addrs.NotDeposed, priorVal, proposedNewVal)\n876: \t}))\n877: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n878: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n879: \t}\n880: \n881: \tvar resp providers.PlanResourceChangeResponse\n882: \tif n.override != nil {\n883: \t\t// Then we have an override to apply for this change. But, overrides\n884: \t\t// only matter when we are creating a resource for the first time as we\n885: \t\t// only apply computed values.\n886: \t\tif priorVal.IsNull() {\n887: \t\t\t// Then we are actually creating something, so let's populate the\n888: \t\t\t// computed values from our override value.\n889: \t\t\toverride, overrideDiags := mocking.PlanComputedValuesForResource(proposedNewVal, schema)\n890: \t\t\tresp = providers.PlanResourceChangeResponse{\n891: \t\t\t\tPlannedState: override,\n892: \t\t\t\tDiagnostics:  overrideDiags,\n893: \t\t\t}\n894: \t\t} else {\n895: \t\t\t// This is an update operation, and we don't actually have any\n896: \t\t\t// computed values that need to be applied.\n897: \t\t\tresp = providers.PlanResourceChangeResponse{\n898: \t\t\t\tPlannedState: proposedNewVal,\n899: \t\t\t}\n900: \t\t}\n901: \t} else {\n902: \t\tresp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n903: \t\t\tTypeName:         n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n904: \t\t\tConfig:           unmarkedConfigVal,\n905: \t\t\tPriorState:       unmarkedPriorVal,\n906: \t\t\tProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,\n907: \t\t\tPriorPrivate:     priorPrivate,\n908: \t\t\tProviderMeta:     metaConfigVal,\n909: \t\t})\n910: \t}\n911: \tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(config.Config, n.Addr.String()))\n912: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n913: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n914: \t}\n915: \n916: \tplannedNewVal := resp.PlannedState\n917: \tplannedPrivate := resp.PlannedPrivate\n918: \n919: \tif plannedNewVal == cty.NilVal {\n920: \t\t// Should never happen. Since real-world providers return via RPC a nil\n921: \t\t// is always a bug in the client-side stub. This is more likely caused\n922: \t\t// by an incompletely-configured mock provider in tests, though.\n923: \t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"PlanResourceChange of %s produced nil value\", n.Addr))\n924: \t}\n925: \n926: \t// We allow the planned new value to disagree with configuration _values_\n927: \t// here, since that allows the provider to do special logic like a\n928: \t// DiffSuppressFunc, but we still require that the provider produces\n929: \t// a value whose type conforms to the schema.\n930: \tfor _, err := range plannedNewVal.Type().TestConformance(schema.ImpliedType()) {\n931: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n932: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n933: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid plan\",\n934: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n935: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n936: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, tfdiags.FormatErrorPrefixed(err, n.Addr.String()),\n937: \t\t\t),\n938: \t\t))\n939: \t}\n940: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n941: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n942: \t}\n943: \n944: \tif errs := objchange.AssertPlanValid(schema, unmarkedPriorVal, unmarkedConfigVal, plannedNewVal); len(errs) > 0 {\n945: \t\tif resp.LegacyTypeSystem {\n946: \t\t\t// The shimming of the old type system in the legacy SDK is not precise\n947: \t\t\t// enough to pass this consistency check, so we'll give it a pass here,\n948: \t\t\t// but we will generate a warning about it so that we are more likely\n949: \t\t\t// to notice in the logs if an inconsistency beyond the type system\n950: \t\t\t// leads to a downstream provider failure.\n951: \t\t\tvar buf strings.Builder\n952: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf,\n953: \t\t\t\t\"[WARN] Provider %q produced an invalid plan for %s, but we are tolerating it because it is using the legacy plugin SDK.\\n    The following problems may be the cause of any confusing errors from downstream operations:\",\n954: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr,\n955: \t\t\t)\n956: \t\t\tfor _, err := range errs {\n957: \t\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"\\n      - %s\", tfdiags.FormatError(err))\n958: \t\t\t}\n959: \t\t\tlog.Print(buf.String())\n960: \t\t} else {\n961: \t\t\tfor _, err := range errs {\n962: \t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n963: \t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n964: \t\t\t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid plan\",\n965: \t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n966: \t\t\t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n967: \t\t\t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, tfdiags.FormatErrorPrefixed(err, n.Addr.String()),\n968: \t\t\t\t\t),\n969: \t\t\t\t))\n970: \t\t\t}\n971: \t\t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n972: \t\t}\n973: \t}\n974: \n975: \tif resp.LegacyTypeSystem {\n976: \t\t// Because we allow legacy providers to depart from the contract and\n977: \t\t// return changes to non-computed values, the plan response may have\n978: \t\t// altered values that were already suppressed with ignore_changes.\n979: \t\t// A prime example of this is where providers attempt to obfuscate\n980: \t\t// config data by turning the config value into a hash and storing the\n981: \t\t// hash value in the state. There are enough cases of this in existing\n982: \t\t// providers that we must accommodate the behavior for now, so for\n983: \t\t// ignore_changes to work at all on these values, we will revert the\n984: \t\t// ignored values once more.\n985: \t\t// A nil schema is passed to processIgnoreChanges to indicate that we\n986: \t\t// don't want to fixup a config value according to the schema when\n987: \t\t// ignoring \"all\", rather we are reverting provider imposed changes.\n988: \t\tplannedNewVal, ignoreChangeDiags = n.processIgnoreChanges(unmarkedPriorVal, plannedNewVal, nil)\n989: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(ignoreChangeDiags)\n990: \t\tif ignoreChangeDiags.HasErrors() {\n991: \t\t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n992: \t\t}\n993: \t}\n994: \n995: \t// Add the marks back to the planned new value -- this must happen after ignore changes\n996: \t// have been processed\n997: \tunmarkedPlannedNewVal := plannedNewVal\n998: \tif len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n999: \t\tplannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n1000: \t}\n1001: \n1002: \t// The provider produces a list of paths to attributes whose changes mean\n1003: \t// that we must replace rather than update an existing remote object.\n1004: \t// However, we only need to do that if the identified attributes _have_\n1005: \t// actually changed -- particularly after we may have undone some of the\n1006: \t// changes in processIgnoreChanges -- so now we'll filter that list to\n1007: \t// include only where changes are detected.\n1008: \treqRep := cty.NewPathSet()\n1009: \tif len(resp.RequiresReplace) > 0 {\n1010: \t\tfor _, path := range resp.RequiresReplace {\n1011: \t\t\tif priorVal.IsNull() {\n1012: \t\t\t\t// If prior is null then we don't expect any RequiresReplace at all,\n1013: \t\t\t\t// because this is a Create action.\n1014: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1015: \t\t\t}\n1016: \n1017: \t\t\tpriorChangedVal, priorPathDiags := hcl.ApplyPath(unmarkedPriorVal, path, nil)\n1018: \t\t\tplannedChangedVal, plannedPathDiags := hcl.ApplyPath(plannedNewVal, path, nil)\n1019: \t\t\tif plannedPathDiags.HasErrors() && priorPathDiags.HasErrors() {\n1020: \t\t\t\t// This means the path was invalid in both the prior and new\n1021: \t\t\t\t// values, which is an error with the provider itself.\n1022: \t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n1023: \t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n1024: \t\t\t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid plan\",\n1025: \t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n1026: \t\t\t\t\t\t\"Provider %q has indicated \\\"requires replacement\\\" on %s for a non-existent attribute path %#v.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n1027: \t\t\t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr, path,\n1028: \t\t\t\t\t),\n1029: \t\t\t\t))\n1030: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1031: \t\t\t}\n1032: \n1033: \t\t\t// Make sure we have valid Values for both values.\n1034: \t\t\t// Note: if the opposing value was of the type\n1035: \t\t\t// cty.DynamicPseudoType, the type assigned here may not exactly\n1036: \t\t\t// match the schema. This is fine here, since we're only going to\n1037: \t\t\t// check for equality, but if the NullVal is to be used, we need to\n1038: \t\t\t// check the schema for th true type.\n1039: \t\t\tswitch {\n1040: \t\t\tcase priorChangedVal == cty.NilVal && plannedChangedVal == cty.NilVal:\n1041: \t\t\t\t// this should never happen without ApplyPath errors above\n1042: \t\t\t\tpanic(\"requires replace path returned 2 nil values\")\n1043: \t\t\tcase priorChangedVal == cty.NilVal:\n1044: \t\t\t\tpriorChangedVal = cty.NullVal(plannedChangedVal.Type())\n1045: \t\t\tcase plannedChangedVal == cty.NilVal:\n1046: \t\t\t\tplannedChangedVal = cty.NullVal(priorChangedVal.Type())\n1047: \t\t\t}\n1048: \n1049: \t\t\t// Unmark for this value for the equality test. If only sensitivity has changed,\n1050: \t\t\t// this does not require an Update or Replace\n1051: \t\t\tunmarkedPlannedChangedVal, _ := plannedChangedVal.UnmarkDeep()\n1052: \t\t\teqV := unmarkedPlannedChangedVal.Equals(priorChangedVal)\n1053: \t\t\tif !eqV.IsKnown() || eqV.False() {\n1054: \t\t\t\treqRep.Add(path)\n1055: \t\t\t}\n1056: \t\t}\n1057: \t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1058: \t\t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1059: \t\t}\n1060: \t}\n1061: \n1062: \t// The user might also ask us to force replacing a particular resource\n1063: \t// instance, regardless of whether the provider thinks it needs replacing.\n1064: \t// For example, users typically do this if they learn a particular object\n1065: \t// has become degraded in an immutable infrastructure scenario and so\n1066: \t// replacing it with a new object is a viable repair path.\n1067: \tmatchedForceReplace := false\n1068: \tfor _, candidateAddr := range forceReplace {\n1069: \t\tif candidateAddr.Equal(n.Addr) {\n1070: \t\t\tmatchedForceReplace = true\n1071: \t\t\tbreak\n1072: \t\t}\n1073: \n1074: \t\t// For \"force replace\" purposes we require an exact resource instance\n1075: \t\t// address to match. If a user forgets to include the instance key\n1076: \t\t// for a multi-instance resource then it won't match here, but we\n1077: \t\t// have an earlier check in NodePlannableResource.Execute that should\n1078: \t\t// prevent us from getting here in that case.\n1079: \t}\n1080: \n1081: \t// Unmark for this test for value equality.\n1082: \teqV := unmarkedPlannedNewVal.Equals(unmarkedPriorVal)\n1083: \teq := eqV.IsKnown() && eqV.True()\n1084: \n1085: \tvar action plans.Action\n1086: \tvar actionReason plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n1087: \tswitch {\n1088: \tcase priorVal.IsNull():\n1089: \t\taction = plans.Create\n1090: \tcase eq && !matchedForceReplace:\n1091: \t\taction = plans.NoOp\n1092: \tcase matchedForceReplace || !reqRep.Empty():\n1093: \t\t// If the user \"forced replace\" of this instance of if there are any\n1094: \t\t// \"requires replace\" paths left _after our filtering above_ then this\n1095: \t\t// is a replace action.\n1096: \t\tif createBeforeDestroy {\n1097: \t\t\taction = plans.CreateThenDelete\n1098: \t\t} else {\n1099: \t\t\taction = plans.DeleteThenCreate\n1100: \t\t}\n1101: \t\tswitch {\n1102: \t\tcase matchedForceReplace:\n1103: \t\t\tactionReason = plans.ResourceInstanceReplaceByRequest\n1104: \t\tcase !reqRep.Empty():\n1105: \t\t\tactionReason = plans.ResourceInstanceReplaceBecauseCannotUpdate\n1106: \t\t}\n1107: \tdefault:\n1108: \t\taction = plans.Update\n1109: \t\t// \"Delete\" is never chosen here, because deletion plans are always\n1110: \t\t// created more directly elsewhere, such as in \"orphan\" handling.\n1111: \t}\n1112: \n1113: \tif action.IsReplace() {\n1114: \t\t// In this strange situation we want to produce a change object that\n1115: \t\t// shows our real prior object but has a _new_ object that is built\n1116: \t\t// from a null prior object, since we're going to delete the one\n1117: \t\t// that has all the computed values on it.\n1118: \t\t//\n1119: \t\t// Therefore we'll ask the provider to plan again here, giving it\n1120: \t\t// a null object for the prior, and then we'll meld that with the\n1121: \t\t// _actual_ prior state to produce a correctly-shaped replace change.\n1122: \t\t// The resulting change should show any computed attributes changing\n1123: \t\t// from known prior values to unknown values, unless the provider is\n1124: \t\t// able to predict new values for any of these computed attributes.\n1125: \t\tnullPriorVal := cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n1126: \n1127: \t\t// Since there is no prior state to compare after replacement, we need\n1128: \t\t// a new unmarked config from our original with no ignored values.\n1129: \t\tunmarkedConfigVal := origConfigVal\n1130: \t\tif origConfigVal.ContainsMarked() {\n1131: \t\t\tunmarkedConfigVal, _ = origConfigVal.UnmarkDeep()\n1132: \t\t}\n1133: \n1134: \t\t// create a new proposed value from the null state and the config\n1135: \t\tproposedNewVal = objchange.ProposedNew(schema, nullPriorVal, unmarkedConfigVal)\n1136: \n1137: \t\tif n.override != nil {\n1138: \t\t\t// In this case, we are always creating the resource so we don't\n1139: \t\t\t// do any validation, and just call out to the mocking library.\n1140: \t\t\toverride, overrideDiags := mocking.PlanComputedValuesForResource(proposedNewVal, schema)\n1141: \t\t\tresp = providers.PlanResourceChangeResponse{\n1142: \t\t\t\tPlannedState: override,\n1143: \t\t\t\tDiagnostics:  overrideDiags,\n1144: \t\t\t}\n1145: \t\t} else {\n1146: \t\t\tresp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n1147: \t\t\t\tTypeName:         n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n1148: \t\t\t\tConfig:           unmarkedConfigVal,\n1149: \t\t\t\tPriorState:       nullPriorVal,\n1150: \t\t\t\tProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,\n1151: \t\t\t\tPriorPrivate:     plannedPrivate,\n1152: \t\t\t\tProviderMeta:     metaConfigVal,\n1153: \t\t\t})\n1154: \t\t}\n1155: \t\t// We need to tread carefully here, since if there are any warnings\n1156: \t\t// in here they probably also came out of our previous call to\n1157: \t\t// PlanResourceChange above, and so we don't want to repeat them.\n1158: \t\t// Consequently, we break from the usual pattern here and only\n1159: \t\t// append these new diagnostics if there's at least one error inside.\n1160: \t\tif resp.Diagnostics.HasErrors() {\n1161: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(config.Config, n.Addr.String()))\n1162: \t\t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1163: \t\t}\n1164: \t\tplannedNewVal = resp.PlannedState\n1165: \t\tplannedPrivate = resp.PlannedPrivate\n1166: \n1167: \t\tif len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n1168: \t\t\tplannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n1169: \t\t}\n1170: \n1171: \t\tfor _, err := range plannedNewVal.Type().TestConformance(schema.ImpliedType()) {\n1172: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n1173: \t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n1174: \t\t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid plan\",\n1175: \t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n1176: \t\t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s%s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n1177: \t\t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr, tfdiags.FormatError(err),\n1178: \t\t\t\t),\n1179: \t\t\t))\n1180: \t\t}\n1181: \t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1182: \t\t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1183: \t\t}\n1184: \t}\n1185: \n1186: \t// If our prior value was tainted then we actually want this to appear\n1187: \t// as a replace change, even though so far we've been treating it as a\n1188: \t// create.\n1189: \tif action == plans.Create && !priorValTainted.IsNull() {\n1190: \t\tif createBeforeDestroy {\n1191: \t\t\taction = plans.CreateThenDelete\n1192: \t\t} else {\n1193: \t\t\taction = plans.DeleteThenCreate\n1194: \t\t}\n1195: \t\tpriorVal = priorValTainted\n1196: \t\tactionReason = plans.ResourceInstanceReplaceBecauseTainted\n1197: \t}\n1198: \n1199: \t// If we plan to write or delete sensitive paths from state,\n1200: \t// this is an Update action.\n1201: \t//\n1202: \t// We need to filter out any marks which may not apply to the new planned\n1203: \t// value before comparison. The one case where a provider is allowed to\n1204: \t// return a different value from the configuration is when a config change\n1205: \t// is not functionally significant and the prior state can be returned. If a\n1206: \t// new mark was also discarded from that config change, it needs to be\n1207: \t// ignored here to prevent an errant update action.\n1208: \tif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n1209: \t\taction = plans.Update\n1210: \t}\n1211: \n1212: \t// As a special case, if we have a previous diff (presumably from the plan\n1213: \t// phases, whereas we're now in the apply phase) and it was for a replace,\n1214: \t// we've already deleted the original object from state by the time we\n1215: \t// get here and so we would've ended up with a _create_ action this time,\n1216: \t// which we now need to paper over to get a result consistent with what\n1217: \t// we originally intended.\n1218: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n1219: \t\tprevChange := *plannedChange\n1220: \t\tif prevChange.Action.IsReplace() && action == plans.Create {\n1221: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] plan: %s treating Create change as %s change to match with earlier plan\", n.Addr, prevChange.Action)\n1222: \t\t\taction = prevChange.Action\n1223: \t\t\tpriorVal = prevChange.Before\n1224: \t\t}\n1225: \t}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n1228: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n1229: \t\treturn h.PostDiff(n.Addr, addrs.NotDeposed, action, priorVal, plannedNewVal)\n1230: \t}))\n1231: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1232: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1233: \t}\n1234: \n1235: \t// Update our return plan\n1236: \tplan := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1237: \t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1238: \t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1239: \t\tPrivate:      plannedPrivate,\n1240: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1241: \t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1242: \t\t\tAction: encoding.\n1247: \t\t\tAfter:           plannedNewVal,\n1248: \t\t\tGeneratedConfig: n.generatedConfigHCL,\n1249: \t\t},\n1250: \t\tActionReason:    actionReason,\n1251: \t\tRequiredReplace: reqRep,\n1252: \t}\n1253: \n1254: \t// Update our return state\n1255: \tstate := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1256: \t\t// We use the special \"planned\" status here to note that this\n1257: \t\t// object's value is not yet complete. Objects with this status\n1258: \t\t// cannot be used during expression evaluation, so the caller\n1259: \t\t// must _also_ record the returned change in the active plan,\n1260: \t\t// which the expression evaluator will use in preference to this\n1261: \t\t// incomplete value recorded in the state.\n1262: \t\tStatus:  states.ObjectPlanned,\n1263: \t\tValue:   plannedNewVal,\n1264: \t\tPrivate: plannedPrivate,\n1265: \t}\n1266: \n1267: \treturn plan, state, keyData, diags\n1268: }\n1269: \n1270: func (n *NodeAbstractResource) processIgnoreChanges(prior, config cty.Value, schema *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1271: \t// ignore_changes only applies when an object already exists, since we\n1272: \t// can't ignore changes to a thing we've not created yet.\n1273: \tif prior.IsNull() {\n1274: \t\treturn config, nil\n1275: \t}\n1276: \n1277: \tignoreChanges := traversalsToPaths(n.Config.Managed.IgnoreChanges)\n1278: \tignoreAll := n.Config.Managed.IgnoreAllChanges\n1279: \n1280: \tif len(ignoreChanges) == 0 && !ignoreAll {\n1281: \t\treturn config, nil\n1282: \t}\n1283: \n1284: \tif ignoreAll {\n1285: \t\t// Legacy providers need up to clean up their invalid plans and ensure\n1286: \t\t// no changes are passed though, but that also means making an invalid\n1287: \t\t// config with computed values. In that case we just don't supply a\n1288: \t\t// schema and return the prior val directly.\n1289: \t\tif schema == nil {\n1290: \t\t\treturn prior, nil\n1291: \t\t}\n1292: \n1293: \t\t// If we are configuration.\n1296: \t\tret, _ := cty.Transform(prior, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1297: \t\t\tattr := schema.AttributeByPath(path)\n1298: \t\t\tif attr != nil && attr.Computed && !attr.Optional {\n1299: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n1300: \t\t\t}\n1301: \n1302: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1303: \t\t})\n1304: \n1305: \t\treturn ret, nil\n1306: \t}\n1307: \n1308: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1309: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1310: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then we'll just let it be.\n1311: \t\treturn config, nil\n1312: \t}\n1313: \n1314: \tret, diags := processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config, ignoreChanges)\n1315: \n1316: \treturn ret, diags\n1317: }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1326: \t}\n1327: \treturn paths\n1328: }\n1329: \n1330: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1331: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1332: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1333: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1334: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1335: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1336: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1337: \t\t\t}\n1338: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseAttr:\n1339: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1340: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1341: \t\t\t}\n1342: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseIndex:\n1343: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.IndexStep{\n1344: \t\t\t\tKey: ts.Key,\n1345: \t\t\t}\n1346: \t\tdefault:\n1347: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported traversal step %#v\", step))\n1348: \t\t}\n1349: \t}\n1350: \treturn path\n1351: }\n1352: \n1353: func processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. This means that the change is stored\n1396: \t\t// here even if our ignored key doesn't change. That is OK since it\n1397: \t\t// won't cause any changes in the transformation, but allows us to skip\n1398: \t\t// breaking up the maps and checking for key existence here too.\n1399: \t\tif !p.RawEquals(c) {\n1400: \t\t\t// there a change to ignore at this path, store the prior value\n1401: \t\t\tignoredValues = append(ignoredValues, ignoreChange{icPath, p, key})\n1402: \t\t}\n1403: \t}\n1404: \n1405: \tif len(ignoredValues) == 0 {\n1406: \t\treturn config, nil\n1407: \t}\n1408: \n1409: \tret, _ := cty.Transform(config, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1410: \t\t// Easy path for when we are only matching the entire value. The only\n1411: \t\t// values we break up for inspection are maps.\n1412: \t\tif !v.Type().IsMapType() {\n1413: \t\t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1414: \t\t\t\tif path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1415: \t\t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1416: \t\t\t\t}\n1417: \t\t\t}\n1418: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1419: \t\t}\n1420: \t\t// We now know this must be a map, so we need to accumulate the values\n1421: \t\t// key-by-key.\n1422: \n1423: \t\tif !v.IsNull() && !v.IsKnown() {\n1424: \t\t\t// since v is not known, we cannot ignore individual keys\n1425: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1426: \t\t}\n1427: \n1428: \t\t// The map values will remain as cty values, so we only need to store\n1429: \t\t// the marks from the outer map itself\n1430: \t\tv, vMarks := v.Unmark()\n1431: \n1432: \t\t// The configMap is the current configuration value, which we will\n1433: \t\t// mutate based on the ignored paths and the prior map value.\n1434: \t\tvar configMap map[string]cty.Value\n1435: \t\tswitch {\n1436: \t\tcase v.IsNull() || v.LengthInt() == 0:\n1437: \t\t\tconfigMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1438: \t\tdefault:\n1439: \t\t\tconfigMap = v.AsValueMap()\n1440: \t\t}\n1441: \n1442: \t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1443: \t\t\tif !path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1444: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1445: \t\t\t}\n1446: \n1447: \t\t\tif ignored.key.IsNull() {\n1448: \t\t\t\t// The map address is confirmed to match at this point,\n1449: \t\t\t\t// so if there is no key, we want the entire map and can\n1450: \t\t\t\t// stop accumulating values.\n1451: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1452: \t\t\t}\n1453: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1454: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1455: \n1456: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1457: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1458: \t\t\t// return null for a key with a null value and for a non-existent\n1459: \t\t\t// key.\n1460: \t\t\tvar priorMap map[string]cty.Value\n1461: \n1462: \t\t\t// We need to drop the marks from the ignored map for handling. We\n1463: \t\t\t// don't need to store these, as we now know the ignored value is\n1464: \t\t\t// only within the map, not the map itself.\n1465: \t\t\tignoredVal, _ := ignored.value.Unmark()\n1466: \n1467: \t\t\tswitch {\n1468: \t\t\tcase ignored.value.IsNull() || ignoredVal.LengthInt() == 0:\n1469: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1470: \t\t\tdefault:\n1471: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = ignoredVal.AsValueMap()\n1472: \t\t\t}\n1473: \n1474: \t\t\tkey := ignored.key.AsString()\n1475: \t\t\tpriorElem, keep := priorMap[key]\n1476: \n1477: \t\t\tswitch {\n1478: \t\t\tcase !keep:\n1479: \t\t\tdefault:\n1483: \t\t\t\tconfigMap[key] = priorElem\n1484: \t\t\t}\n1485: \t\t}\n1486: \n1487: \t\tvar newVal cty.Value\n1488: \t\tswitch {\n1489: \t\tcase len(configMap) > 0:\n1490: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapVal(configMap)\n1491: \t\tcase v.IsNull():\n1492: \t\t\t// if the config value was null, and no values remain in the map,\n1493: \t\t\t// reset the value to null.\n1494: \t\t\tnewVal = v\n1495: \t\tdefault:\n1496: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapValEmpty(v.Type().ElementType())\n1497: \t\t}\n1498: \n1499: \t\tif len(vMarks) > 0 {\n1500: \t\t\tnewVal = newVal.WithMarks(vMarks)\n1501: \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A previously evaluated configVal can be passed in, or a new one is generated\n1510: // from the resource configuration.\n1511: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) readDataSource(ctx EvalContext, configVal cty.Value) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1512: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1513: \tvar newVal cty.Value\n1514: \n1515: \tconfig := *n.Config\n1516: \n1517: \tprovider, errors here, we still want to\n2030: \t\t// identify these diags has having been generated from a check block.\n2031: \t\treadDiags = tfdiags.OverrideAll(readDiags, tfdiags.Warning, func() tfdiags.DiagnosticExtraWrapper {\n2032: \t\t\treturn &addrs.CheckRuleDiagnosticExtra{\n2033: \t\t\t\tCheckRule: addrs.NewCheckRule(addr, addrs.CheckDataResource, 0),\n2034: \t\t\t}\n2035: \t\t})\n2036: \n2037: \t\t// If no errors, just remember to report this as a success and continue\n2038: \t\t// as normal.\n2039: \t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckResult(addr, addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, evalApplyProvisioners determines if provisioners need to be run, and if so\n2056: // executes the provisioners for a resource and returns an updated error if\n2057: // provisioning fails.\n2058: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2059: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2060: \n2061: \tif state == nil {\n2062: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s has no state, so skipping provisioners\", n.Addr)\n2063: \t\treturn nil\n2064: \t}\n2065: \tif when == configs.ProvisionerWhenCreate && !createNew {\n2066: \t\t// If we're not creating a new resource, then don't run provisioners\n2067: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] in provisioning an object that is already tainted, since\n2072: \t\t// it's going to get recreated on the next apply anyway.\n2073: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s is tainted, so don't do anything\n2080: \t\treturn nil\n2081: \t}\n2082: \n2083: \t// Call pre hook\n2084: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n2085: \t\treturn h.PreProvisionInstance(n.Addr, state.Value)\n2086: \t}))\n2087: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n2088: \t\treturn diags\n2089: \t}\n2090: \n2091: \t// If there are no errors, then we append it to our output \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s provisioning failed, but we will continue anyway at the caller's request\", n.Addr)\n2096: \t\treturn diags\n2097: \t}\n2098: \n2099: \t// Call post hook\n2100: \treturn diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n2101: \t\treturn h.PostProvisionInstance(n.Addr, state.Value)\n2102: \t}))\n2103: }\n2104: \n2105: // filterProvisioners []*configs.Provisioner {\n2108: \t// Fast path the zero case\n2109: \tif config == nil || config.Managed == nil {\n2110: \t\treturn nil\n2111: \t}\n2112: \n2113: \tif len(config.Managed.Provisioners) == 0 {\n2114: \t\treturn nil\n2115: \t}\n2116: \n2117: \tresult := make([]*configs.Provisioner, 0, len(config.Managed.Provisioners))\n2118: \tfor _, p := range config.Managed.Provisioners {\n2119: resource.\n2128: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, when configs.ProvisionerWhen, provs []*configs.Provisioner) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2129: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2130: \n2131: \t// this self is only used for destroy provisioner evaluation, and must\n2132: \t// refer to the last known value of the Now I have a complete picture. Let me trace through the flow:\n\n1. **State Decoding** (instance_object_src.go, line 77-104):\n   - When state is decoded from disk, only `AttrSensitivePaths` marks are applied (lines 89-91)\n   - These are the marks that were stored in the state file\n\n2. **State Encoding** (instance_object.go, line 94-137):\n   - When state is encoded to disk, marks are extracted from the value (line 98)\n   - Only those extracted marks are stored in `AttrSensitivePaths` (line 131)\n\n3. **The Problem**:\n   - Schema marks are NEVER added to values before they are stored in state\n   - So schema marks NEVER make it into the state file\n   - The only marks stored in state are those from sensitive variable references\n\n4. **The Compensating Workaround**:\n   - In `evaluate.go` GetResource (lines 714-723), schema marks are ADDED when reading values for expression evaluation\n   - This is the ONLY place schema marks are applied to values read from state\n   - But this asymmetry causes phantom diffs\n\n5. **The Phantom Diff Mechanism**:\n   - In node_resource_abstract_instance.go plan() method:\n     - Line 869: `unmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` - extracts marks from prior state\n     - Lines 999-1000: `plannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)` - adds marks from config back\n     - Line 1208: Checks if marks differ, and if so, changes NoOp to Update\n\n6. **The Manifestation**:\n   - When a resource is refreshed (read back from provider):\n     - The provider response has no marks\n     - The prior state used in plan also has no Let me compile what I've found:\n\n## Root Cause Analysis\n\nThe phantom in-place updates occur because of an asymmetry between:\n1. How marks (sensitivity information) from the provider schema are applied during evaluation\n2. How marks are stored in the state file\n\n### The Mechanism:\n\n1. **State Storage** (instance_object.go, Encode method, line 94-137):\n   - When a resource value is encoded for storage in state, ALL marks are extracted (line 98)\n   - Only those extracted marks are stored in `AttrSensitivePaths` (line 131)\n   - Problem: Schema-defined sensitivity marks are NEVER added to values before encoding, so they're never stored\n\n2. **State Retrieval** (instance_object_src.go, Decode method, line 77-104):\n   - When state is decoded from disk, ONLY the stored `AttrSensitivePaths` marks are reapplied (lines 89-91)\n   - Schema marks are NOT applied during decoding\n\n3. **Compensating Workaround** (evaluate.go, GetResource, line 714-723):\n   - When values are read from state FOR EXPRESSION EVALUATION, schema marks are explicitly added (line 721)\n   - This is the ONLY place where schema sensitivity is applied to state values\n   - But this creates an asymmetry:\n     - Values IN STATE don't have schema marks\n     - Values USED FOR EVALUATION do have schema marks\n\n4. **Refresh Path** (node_resource_abstract_instance.go, refresh, line 578-723):\n   - Prior state is unmarked (line 625), extracting only the marks that are in state\n   - Provider response (newState) is also unmarked (no marks from provider)\n   - Marks are reapplied to the returned state (line 719), but only the marks that were extracted from the original state\n   - Result: Refreshed state STILL has incomplete marks (missing schema-defined marks)\n   \n5. **Plan Path** (node_resource_abstract_instance.go, plan, line 725-1250):\n   - Prior marks are extracted via `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` (line 869), capturing only what's stored in state\n   - Planned value gets marked with these incomplete paths (line 999)\n   - The equality check on unmarked values passes (line 1082), but then mark comparison at line 1208 detects a difference\n   - Since schema marks were applied to the planned value during evaluation but aren't in the prior state's marks, the system incorrectly flags this as requiring an update\n   - The root issue: state preservation doesn't include schema-defined marks, so the comparison is fundamentally asymmetric\n\n6. **JSON Output Discrepancy** (jsonplan/plan.go, jsonstate/state.go):\n   - Schema marks get explicitly added when generating JSON output (lines 418-420, 447-449), creating sensitivity information that differs from what's actually stored in state\n   - This means the JSON representation shows complete mark information while the persisted state is incomplete\n\nThe problem traces back through the entire flow: providers return unmarked values, state encoding only preserves marks already present on the value (missing schema marks), and when the {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016uoq7wk8unYz2H3M2hW2UL","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01EqqwF9jwDEbhmnXps7sNJu","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because provider schema sensitivity marks are never stored in state, creating an asymmetry where the evaluator adds these marks during expression evaluation but the plan comparison uses incomplete marks from the state file.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Core Issue**: Schema-defined sensitive attribute marks are not persisted in the state file, but they ARE applied during expression evaluation. This causes the mark sets to differ between what's stored in state and what's used during planning, triggering spurious update actions.\n\n**Mechanism**:\n- When resource values are encoded for state storage (`instance_object.go`), only marks already present on the value are extracted. Schema-defined sensitivity is never added to values before encoding, so it never makes it into `AttrSensitivePaths`.\n- During plan operations, the comparison checks both value equality and mark equality (`node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`). When the mark sets differ (because schema marks are absent from the prior state's `priorPaths`), Terraform changes the action from NoOp to Update, even though the actual attribute values are identical.\n- The compensating workaround in `evaluate.go:GetResource()` adds schema marks during expression evaluation, but this only masks the problem for expression evaluation—not for plan comparison.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. State Encoding without Schema Marks\n**File**: `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137`\n\n```go\n// Line 98: Extract marks from the value (but schema marks were never added)\nval, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Lines 129-131: Only extracted marks are stored\nreturn &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n    // ...\n    AttrSensitivePaths: pvm,  // <- Only contains marks that were on the value\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**Problem**: Schema marks are never added to the value before encoding, so only variable-reference marks make it into the state file.\n\n### 2. State Decoding without Schema Marks\n**File**: `internal/states/instance_object_src.go:77-104`\n\n```go\n// Lines 89-91: Only apply marks that are stored in state\nif os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)\n}\n```\n\n**Problem**: Schema marks are not reapplied because they're not in the state file.\n\n### 3. Compensating Workaround in Expression Evaluation\n**File**: `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:714-723`\n\n```go\n// Lines 718-722: Schema marks ARE added during expression evaluation\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    // <- Schema marks are explicitly computed here\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Insight**: This is the ONLY place where schema marks are applied to values read from state. It creates an asymmetry where:\n- Values stored IN STATE lack schema marks\n- Values used FOR EVALUATION have schema marks\n\n### 4. Incomplete Marks in Refresh Path\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:578-723`\n\n```go\n// Lines 620-626: Extract marks from prior state\npriorVal := state.Value\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n\n// Lines 636-642: Call provider with unmarked value\nresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n    TypeName:   n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    PriorState: priorVal,  // <- Unmarked, no schema marks\n    // ...\n})\n\n// Lines 718-720: Reapply only the extracted marks\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n```\n\n**Problem**: `priorPaths` only contains marks from the state file, which lacks schema-defined marks. The refreshed state is returned without schema marks.\n\n### 5. Phantom Update Detection in Plan\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1199-1210`\n\n```go\n// Lines 1199-1210: THE PHANTOM UPDATE TRIGGER\n// If our prior value was tainted then we actually want this to appear\n// as a replace change, even though so far we've been treating it as a\n// create.\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**This is where phantom updates are created**:\n- Line 1082: `eqV := unmarkedPlannedNewVal.Equals(unmarkedPriorVal)` passes (values are identical)\n- Line 1090: Action would normally be `plans.NoOp`\n- Line 1208: But the mark comparison fails because:\n  - `filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths)` = marks from config (which may include no schema marks)\n  - `priorPaths` = marks from prior state (which definitely lacks schema marks)\n  - If they differ, action changes to Update\n- **Result**: Phantom Update even though values are identical\n\n### 6. Incomplete Sensitivity in JSON Output\n**Files**: `internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go:410-455` and `internal/command/jsonstate/state.go:400-460`\n\n```go\n// Lines 418-420 (jsonplan/plan.go): Schema marks ARE added for JSON output\nmarks := rc.BeforeValMarks\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.Before, nil)...)\n}\n\n// Lines 447-449: Schema marks added for after value too\nmarks := rc.AfterValMarks\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.After, nil)...)\n}\n```\n\n**Manifestation**:\n- JSON plan output shows schema-defined sensitivity marks (via explicit `schema.ValueMarks()` call)\n- But these marks are not stored in the state file\n- `terraform show -json` on state shows incomplete `sensitive_values` (missing schema-defined paths)\n- This creates a mismatch between what users see in JSON output and what's actually in state\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/states/`** - State serialization\n   - `instance_object.go` - Value encoding for state storage\n   - `instance_object_src.go` - Value decoding from state\n\n2. **`internal/terraform/`** - Graph evaluation and planning\n   - `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` - Resource instance graph node, handles refresh and plan operations\n   - `evaluate.go` - Expression evaluation with compensating workaround\n   - `marks.go` - Mark comparison utilities\n\n3. **`internal/command/`** - CLI output generation\n   - `jsonplan/plan.go` - Plan JSON serialization with explicit schema mark addition\n   - `jsonstate/state.go` - State JSON serialization with explicit schema mark addition\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider Response** → Value without any marks (providers don't add marks)\n2. **Plan Processing** → Marks are extracted from config expressions via `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`\n3. **State Encoding** → Value with only extracted marks is persisted (schema marks never added before encoding)\n4. **State File Storage** → `AttrSensitivePaths` contains only variable-reference marks, not schema marks\n5. **State Decoding** → Only stored marks (variable-reference) are reapplied to value\n6. **Refresh Operation** → Prior marks extracted from state (incomplete, missing schema marks)\n7. **Plan Operation** → Marks comparison in line 1208 finds `priorPaths` incomplete\n8. **Sensitivity Check** → Mark mismatch triggers action change from NoOp to Update\n9. **Phantom Update** → User sees \"will be updated in-place\" despite identical values\n10. **JSON Output** → Explicit schema mark addition for JSON masks the issue partially, but state lacks marks\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy**: Add schema-defined sensitivity marks to resource values BEFORE they are encoded to state.\n\n**Implementation Steps**:\n\n1. **In state encoding** (`instance_object.go:Encode`):\n   - Before calling `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` (line 98), add schema marks to the value\n   - This requires passing the schema to the Encode method\n   - Ensure schema marks are included in the extracted `pvm`\n\n2. **Schema availability**:\n   - The Encode method needs access to the resource schema to determine which attributes should be marked as sensitive\n   - This requires changes to the method signature or context\n\n3. **State compatibility**:\n   - Once schema marks are stored in state files, old state files (without these marks) will need to be handled gracefully during decoding\n   - The current code in `instance_object_src.go` should be forward-compatible since it applies any marks found in `AttrSensitivePaths`\n\n4. **Remove compensating workaround**:\n   - Once schema marks are properly stored in state, the workaround in `evaluate.go:GetResource()` (lines 718-722) can be simplified or removed\n   - Values read from state will already have the correct marks\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Enable detailed logging in the mark comparison (line 1208 of `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`)\n2. Compare `priorPaths` and `filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths)` to confirm the difference\n3. Verify that schema-defined attribute paths are missing from `priorPaths`\n4. Check that the same attributes appear in JSON output sensitivity marks (via `schema.ValueMarks()`)\n\n**Testing**:\n\n1. Create test resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes\n2. After successful apply, immediately run plan and verify no phantom updates\n3. Verify state file contains the complete set of sensitive paths\n4. Confirm JSON output matches state sensitivity information\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":530,"cache_read_input_tokens":73092,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":530},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"07ed87d9-ec8c-45de-9f03-709b3e2ee94f","uuid":"0e51a98e-c4c9-4f21-b56c-e5498eb67011"}

CLI output generation\n   - `jsonplan/plan.go` - Plan JSON serialization with explicit schema mark addition\n   - `jsonstate/state.go` - State JSON serialization with explicit schema mark addition\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider Response** → Value without any marks (providers don't add marks)\n2. **Plan Processing** → Marks are extracted from config expressions via `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`\n3. **State Encoding** → Value with only extracted marks is persisted (schema marks never added before encoding)\n4. **State File Storage** → `AttrSensitivePaths` contains only variable-reference marks, not schema marks\n5. **State Decoding** → Only stored marks (variable-reference) are reapplied to value\n6. **Refresh Operation** → Prior marks extracted from state (incomplete, missing schema marks)\n7. **Plan Operation** → Marks comparison in line 1208 finds `priorPaths` incomplete\n8. **Sensitivity Check** → Mark mismatch triggers action change from NoOp to Update\n9. **Phantom Update** → User sees \"will be updated in-place\" despite identical values\n10. **JSON Output** → Explicit schema mark addition for JSON masks the issue partially, but state lacks marks\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy**: Add schema-defined sensitivity marks to resource values BEFORE they are encoded to state.\n\n**Implementation Steps**:\n\n1. **In state encoding** (`instance_object.go:Encode`):\n   - Before calling `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` (line 98), add schema marks to the value\n   - This requires passing the schema to the Encode method\n   - Ensure schema marks are included in the extracted `pvm`\n\n2. **Schema availability**:\n   - The Encode method needs access to the resource schema to determine which attributes should be marked as sensitive\n   - This requires changes to the method signature or context\n\n3. **State compatibility**:\n   - Once schema marks are stored in state files, old state files (without these marks) will need to be handled gracefully during decoding\n   - The current code in `instance_object_src.go` should be forward-compatible since it applies any marks found in `AttrSensitivePaths`\n\n4. **Remove compensating workaround**:\n   - Once schema marks are properly stored in state, the workaround in `evaluate.go:GetResource()` (lines 718-722) can be simplified or removed\n   - Values read from state will already have the correct marks\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Enable detailed logging in the mark comparison (line 1208 of `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`)\n2. Compare `priorPaths` and `filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths)` to confirm the difference\n3. Verify that schema-defined attribute paths are missing from `priorPaths`\n4. Check that the same attributes appear in JSON output sensitivity marks (via `schema.ValueMarks()`)\n\n**Testing**:\n\n1. Create test resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes\n2.
